Waqf — Endowment

12 min
Amputation for Theft from Waqf – Dispute and Refinement
Later scholarly discussion on whether amputation applies for theft from waqf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the corpus and income of waqf and state the conditions under which amputation applies according to later Hanafi fatwa.

Core Idea
Amputation for theft from waqf depends on ownership: corpus vs. income, private vs. public waqf.

The initial Hanafi ruling on theft from waqf was no amputation because waqf has no owner. However, later scholars refined this by distinguishing between the corpus and income, and between private and public waqf. In this lesson, you will explore this critical refinement and apply it to various scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling and its basis
The matn originally stated no amputation for theft from waqf property, as waqf is considered ownerless and hadd requires an owner.
This is the starting point of the dispute.
2
Recognize the corpus vs. income distinction
Later scholars noted that the corpus (raqabah) remains on the ownership of the waqif by legal fiction, while income (ghallah) belongs to the beneficiaries. Amputation may apply to theft of the corpus if the mutawalli claims.
Al-Ramli and others emphasize this distinction.
3
Understand the role of the mutawalli's valid hand
A mutawalli with a valid hand (yad sahihah) can be a litigant and request hadd. This applies when the waqf is for specific beneficiaries.
The mutawalli represents the owner or beneficiaries.
4
Distinguish private waqf from public waqf
For private waqf (e.g., for children), the income is owned by individuals, so amputation applies. For public waqf (e.g., for the poor), it resembles bayt al-mal and no amputation if the thief is a beneficiary.
Public waqf like a mosque's income has no specific owner.
5
Determine the mufta bihi ruling
The operative ruling is that amputation applies for theft from private waqf corpus or income if the mutawalli claims, but not for public waqf or if the thief is a beneficiary.
This is based on later fatwa works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وأما مال الوقف الخ) قال المقدسي في شرحه صرحوا بأن متولي الوقف يقطع بطلبه، ذكره في التبيين والفتح ونحوهما، وطلبه إنما هو في الوقف .اهـ. وقال الرملي : صرح ابن ملك في شرح المجمع من بحث الخاص بأنه لو سرق مال الوقف من المتولي يجب القطع وسيأتي في شرح قوله «ولو مودعاً والأصل فيه أن كل من كان له يد صحيحة يملك الخصومة إلى أن قال : فللمالك أن يخاصم السارق ثم قال : ومتولي المسجد ثم قال : فتعتبر خصومتهم في ثبوت ولاية الاسترداد وفي حق القطع، فهو صريح فيه ويلوح الفرق بين نحو حصر المسجد وغيرها فتأمل اهـ. ونحوه في حواشي أبي السعود عن شيخه، ولعل الفرق هو أن الوقف باقي على ملك الواقف حكماً الإمام كما يأتي في محله لكن هذا يظهر في رقبة الوقف، أما غلته فلا وعلى هذا فعدم القطع في حصر المسجد لعدم المالك لكونها من غلة الوقف بخلاف رقبة الوقف كما لو وقف على أولاده مثلاً جرى به التعامل من المنقولات وقد صرحوا بأن غلة الوقف ملك المستحقين وأنها أمانة تحت يد الناظر، فعلى هذا يكون للمتولي يد صحيحة عليها فله القطع بها لكن ينبغي عدم القطع فيما لو كان وقفاً على العامة كالوقف على الفقراء فإنه مثل بيت المال إذا كان السارق فقيراً، وأما وقف المسجد فالظاهر أنه ليس كذلك لأنه ليس لأحد تناول شيء من غلته لأنها تصرف في منافع المسجد إلا أن يكون له وظيفة في المسجد. قوله : (وفيه أن ابن أبي ليلى) أي وفي المجتبى
His saying: (As for waqf property...) Al-Maqdisi said in his commentary: They explicitly stated that the mutawalli of the waqf can request amputation, mentioned in al-Tabyin and al-Fath and similar works. And his request pertains to the waqf. End quote. Al-Ramli said: Ibn Malik explicitly stated in Sharh al-Majma' from the section on khas (private) that if someone steals waqf property from the mutawalli, amputation is obligatory. It will come in the explanation of his saying 'and even if it is a deposit' and the principle is that whoever has a valid hand (yad sahihah) can be a litigant, until he said: So the owner can sue the thief, then he said: and the mutawalli of the mosque, then he said: So their litigation is considered in establishing the authority of recovery and for the right of amputation. This is explicit in it, and the difference between something like the mat of a mosque and other things becomes apparent, so ponder. End quote. Similar is in the marginal notes of Abu al-Sa'ud from his shaykh. Perhaps the difference is that the waqf remains on the ownership of the waqif by rule (hukman) according to the Imam, as will come in its place, but this appears regarding the corpus (`ayn) of the waqf, not its income. On this basis, there is no amputation for the mat of the mosque due to the absence of an owner because it is from the income (ghallah) of the waqf, unlike the corpus. For example, if one makes a waqf for his children, dealing in movable properties is customary, and they have stated that the income of the waqf is the property of the beneficiaries and it is an amanah under the hand of the nazir. Accordingly, the mutawalli has a valid hand over it, so he can have amputation. But it is appropriate not to amputate if it is a waqf for the general public, like a waqf for the poor, because it is like bayt al-mal if the thief is poor. As for the waqf of the mosque, it seems it is not like that because no one may take anything from its income, as it is spent on the benefits of the mosque, unless he has a function in the mosque. His saying: (And in it that Ibn Abi Layla...) i.e., in al-Mujtaba.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a later discussion (hāshiyah-style) about amputation for theft from waqf property. The initial ruling in the matn had indicated no amputation due to lack of an owner. However, later scholars like al-Maqdisi, al-Ramli, and Ibn Malik refine this: the mutawalli (custodian) can request amputation if he has a valid hand (yad sahihah) over the property. The key distinction is between the corpus (raqabah) of the waqf and its income (ghallah). For the corpus, since it is considered to remain on the ownership of the waqif by legal fiction (hukman), there may be an owner. For the income (e.g., mats of a mosque), there is no specific owner, so no amputation. However, if the waqf is for specific beneficiaries (e.g., children), the income is their property, and the mutawalli can claim and have amputation. If it is a public waqf for the poor, it resembles bayt al-mal, and if the thief is poor, no amputation. The discussion shows the intricate development of Hanafi fiqh on the issue of waqf and hadd.

Key Terms
مال الوقف (mal al-waqf): Property that has been endowed (waqf), which may have a corpus (raqabah) and income (ghallah).
المتولي (al-mutawalli): The custodian or manager of a waqf.
الغلَّة (al-ghallah): The income or produce generated from waqf property.
يد صحيحة (yad sahihah): A legally valid hand or possession, enabling the holder to be a litigant and claim rights.
رقبة (raqabah): The corpus or principal of a waqf property, as opposed to its income.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to later Hanafi fatwa, can the mutawalli of a waqf for orphans request amputation for a thief who steals from the waqf income?
A) No, because waqf property has no owner.
B) Yes, because the income belongs to the orphans and the mutawalli has a valid hand over it.
C) Only if the thief is not poor.
D) No, because amputation is only for theft from individuals.

Key Takeaway
Amputation for theft from waqf is not categorically denied; it depends on the nature of the property (corpus vs. income) and the type of waqf (private vs. public).

Analogy of Spoils to Salaries of Imam and Mu'adhdhin
Critical refinement of an analogy and settling an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two Hanafi views on the inheritance of an imam's stipend and state the preferred view with its basis.

Core Idea
An imam's stipend is inherited because its wage aspect dominates over its gift aspect.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: does the waqf stipend of an imam or mu'adhdhin pass to his heirs upon his death? The conflict hinges on whether the stipend is treated as a wage (ujra) or a gift (ṣila). Al-Bughya and later fatwas side with the wage analogy, making the stipend inheritable.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the two positions
Identify the contested ruling: whether the stipend of an imam/mu'adhdhin is inherited or forfeited upon death. Note the two views: one treats it as a gift (ṣila) that lapses, the other as wages (ujra) that are inherited.
2
Identify the proofs for each view
The gift view: stipends from waqf are voluntary gifts, so they lapse at death. The wage view: the stipend is compensation for services, so it is akin to earned wages and is inherited.
The wage view is supported by later fatwas allowing hiring for worship.
3
Examine the tarjih mechanism
Al-Bughya gives precedence to the wage aspect, and later mutā'akhkhirūn fatawa support this. The text notes that the analogy to spoils (which are not inherited after iḥrāz) is rejected for stipends.
The authority weight is fatawa_mutakhkhirin.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
If the imam dies before collecting, the practical consequence is: according to the gift view, the stipend is forfeited to the waqf; according to the wage view, it goes to his heirs.
5
Critique the spoils analogy
The passage criticizes the analogy drawn between spoil shares (after iḥrāz) and stipends because spoil shares are rights not gifts or wages, making the analogy invalid.
This critical refinement clarifies the correct legal classification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (قياساً على مسألة (الغنيمة قال في النهر أقول في الدرر والغرر عن فوائد صاحب المحيط : للإمام والمؤذن وقف فلم يستوفيا حتى ماتا سقط لأنه في معنى الصلة، وكذا القاضي، وقيل: لا يسقط لأنه كالأجرة اهـ. وجزم في البغية بأنه يورث بخلاف رزق ،القاضي وأنت خبير بأن ما يأخذه القاضي ليس صلة كما هو ظاهر ولا أجراً لأن مثل هذه العبادة لم يقل أحد بجواز الاستئجار عليها بخلاف ما يأخذه الإمام والمؤذن فإنه لا ينفك عنهما، فبالنظر إلى الأجرة يورث ما يستحق إذا استحق غير مقيد بظهور الغلة وقبضها في يد الناظر وبالنظر إلى الصلة لا يورث وإن قبضه الناظر قبل الموت، وبهذا عرفت أن القياس على الغنيمة غير صحيح وسيأتي لهذا مزيد وبيان في الوقف إن شاء الله تعالى اهـ ما في النهر. ولم أر له في الوقف ذكراً لهذه المسألة، وكذا لم يذكرها المؤلف هناك أيضاً. هذا وقول النهر «إن ما يأخذه القاضي ليس صلة مخالف لما صرح به في الهداية قبيل الردة وسيذكره المؤلف هناك أيضاً. نعم ما يأخذه الإمام ونحوه فيه معنى الصلة ومعنى الأجرة، والظاهر أن ذلك منشأ الخلاف المحكي في الدرر لكن ما جزم به في البغية يقتضي ترجيح جانب الأجرة في حقه وهو ظاهر لا سيما على ما أفتى به المتأخرون من جواز الأجرة على الأذان والإمامة والتعليم. وعن والله تعالى أعلم مشى العلامة الطرسوسي على أن المدرس ونحوه إذا مات في أثناء السنة يعطى بقدر ما باشر ويسقط الباقي بخلاف الوقف على الأولاد والذرية فإنه إذا مات مستحق منهم يعتبر في حقه
His statement: 'by analogy to the spoil issue' – he said in al-Nahr: I say in al-Durar wa al-Ghurar from the benefits of the author of al-Muḥīṭ: there is a waqf for the imam and mu'adhdhin, and they did not take it until they died; it is dropped because it is in the sense of a gift, and likewise the judge. And it is said: it is not dropped because it is like wages. And in al-Bughya he asserted that it is inherited, unlike the salary of the judge. And you know that what the judge takes is not a gift, as is apparent, nor wages, because no one has said that hiring for such worship is permissible, unlike what the imam and mu'adhdhin take, for it is inseparable from them. So with regard to wages, what is deserved is inherited if it is deserved without restriction by the appearance of revenue and its receipt in the hand of the trustee; and with regard to the gift, it is not inherited even if the trustee took it before death. By this you know that the analogy to spoils is not correct, and further detail will come in waqf, God willing. And I did not see for him mention of this issue in waqf, nor did the author mention it there. This and the statement of al-Nahr that 'what the judge takes is not a gift' contradicts what was stated in al-Hidayah near the chapter on apostasy, and the author will mention it there. Yes, what the imam and similar take has both a sense of gift and wages; apparently that is the source of the disagreement reported in al-Durar, but what al-Bughya asserted implies preferring the wage aspect in his case, which is apparent, especially according to the later fatwas permitting wages for adhān, imāma, and teaching. And God knows best. Al-Allāma al-Ṭarsūsī followed that the teacher and similar, if he dies during the year, is given according to what he performed, and the rest is dropped, unlike the waqf for children and descendants, for if a beneficiary dies, it is considered in his case.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage critically examines the analogy drawn between spoil shares after iḥrāz and the stipends (rāz) of religious functionaries like the imam and mu'adhdhin. The author of al-Nahr argues that the analogy is flawed. Stipends from waqf can be considered either as a gift (ṣila) or as wages (ujra). If it is a gift, it is not inherited; if wages, it is inherited. The judge's stipend is not a gift nor wages (since hiring for worship is not allowed), so it is not inherited. The imam's and mu'adhdhin's stipends have both aspects, leading to different opinions. The author asserts that al-Bughya gives precedence to the wage aspect, so it is inherited. The author also notes that al-Nahr's claim that the judge's stipend is not a gift contradicts al-Hidayah. He concludes that the analogy to spoils is not correct because the spoil share after iḥrāz is a right, not a gift or wage. He also mentions the fatwa of al-Ṭarsūsī on teachers.

Key Terms
الصلة (aṣ-ṣila): A gift or gratuity not considered wages.
الأجرة (al-ujra): Wages for services rendered.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in the text, what is the ruling on the stipend of an imam who dies before collecting it?
A) It is forfeited because it is a gift
B) It is inherited by his heirs because it is like wages
C) It goes to the waqf fund
D) It depends on the imam's contract

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that the waqf stipend of an imam or mu'adhdhin is inherited, because the wage aspect is predominant.

Definition of Waqf and the Dispute on Ownership
Defines waqf linguistically and legally, presents internal Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of waqf according to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and explain the difference in legal ownership.

Core Idea
Waqf restricts the corpus while giving charity with the usufruct — but whose ownership remains?

How does Islamic law define an endowment? While linguistically it means restriction, jurists differ on what happens to the property's ownership. In this lesson, we unpack the Hanafi definition of waqf and the classic disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic meaning
The word waqf linguistically means 'restriction' (habs). Confirm this from the Qamus citation.
Some dialect variants are mentioned but the standard is waqf.
2
State Abu Hanifa's legal definition
According to Abu Hanifa, waqf is restricting the corpus (habs al-ayn) while retaining ownership in the waqif, and donating the usufruct (al-tasadduq bi al-manfa'ah).
This is the definition in the matn.
3
State the Sahibayn's legal definition
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, waqf is restricting the corpus to the rule of Allah's ownership; the waqif's ownership is removed.
This view is considered mufta bihi.
4
Understand the practical consequence
Under Abu Hanifa, the waqif could potentially reclaim the property (though judicial decree is needed). Under the Sahibayn, the property becomes irrevocably dedicated to God.
The later school preference is based on preventing revocation.
5
Note the additional nuance on beneficiaries
Waqf can be upon the rich without immediate charity, because ultimately a perpetual pious purpose is required.
This is explained in Fath al-Qadir and al-Dhakhira.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوقف
حبس العين على ملك الواقف والتصدق بالمنفعة والملك يزول بالقضاء لا إلى
كتاب الوقف
مناسبته للشركة باعتبار أن المقصود بكل منهما الانتفاع بما يزيد على أصل المال، وله معنى لغوي وشرعي وسبب ومحل وشرائط وركن وأحكام ومحاسن وصفة. فمعناه في اللغة الحبس قال في القاموس. وقف الدار حبسه كأوقفه وهذه لغة رديئة .اهـ. وأما معناه شرعاً فما أفاده قوله : (حبس) العين على ملك الواقف والتصدق بالمنفعة) يعني عند أبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه، وعندهما هو حبس العين على حكم ملك الله تعالى وزاد في فتح القدير على كلام المصنف أو صرف منفعتها على من أحب قال : لأن الوقف يصح لمن يحب من الأغنياء بلا قصد القربة وهو وإن كان لا بد في آخره من القربة كشرط التأبيد وهو بذلك كالفقراء ومصالح المسجد لكنه يكون وقفاً قبل انقراض الأغنياء بلا تصدق اهـ. وقد يقال : إن الوقف على الغني تصدق بالمنفعة لأن الصدقة كما تكون على الفقراء تكون على الأغنياء وإن كان التصدق على الغني مجازاً عن الهبة عند بعضهم. وصرح في الذخيرة بأن في التصدق على الغني نوع قربة دون قربة الفقير وعرفه شمس الأئمة السرخسي بأنه حبس المملوك عن الغير وسببه إرادة محبوب النفس في الدنيا ببر الأحباب وفي الآخرة بالتقرب إلى رب الأرباب جل وعز. ومحله المال المتقوم
Book of Waqf: Restricting the corpus to the ownership of the waqif and giving away the usufruct as charity; ownership is removed by judicial decree, not to... Book of Waqf: Its appropriateness with partnership is that the purpose of each is benefiting from what exceeds the original capital. It has a linguistic and legal meaning, cause, locus, conditions, pillar, rulings, virtues, and description. Its linguistic meaning is restriction. The Qamus said: 'Waqf of a house means to restrict it, as does awqafahu, but this is a poor usage.' End. As for its legal meaning, it is what his statement (restricting the corpus to the ownership of the waqif and giving away the usufruct) indicates, meaning according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is restricting the corpus to the rule of Allah Almighty's ownership. In Fath al-Qadir, he added to the author's words: 'or directing its benefit to whom he wishes,' because waqf is valid for whomever he wishes among the rich without intending piety, and although it must ultimately involve piety such as the condition of perpetuity, and it is thus like the poor and mosque interests, but it becomes waqf before the extinction of the rich without charity. End. And it may be said that waqf upon the rich is charity of benefit because charity may be upon the rich as upon the poor, although charity upon the rich is metaphorical for gift according to some. In al-Dhakhira, it is explicitly stated that there is a type of piety in charity upon the rich, but less than charity upon the poor. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi defined it as restricting owned property from others. Its cause is the desire for what is beloved in this world through kindness to loved ones, and in the Hereafter through drawing near to the Lord of lords, Glorious and Exalted. Its locus is valuable property.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage defines the legal concept of waqf (endowment) in the Hanafi school. It opens by explaining the genre and the relationship with partnership. The linguistic meaning is 'restriction' (حبس). The legal meaning differs between Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to Abu Hanifa, waqf means restricting the corpus while retaining ownership in the waqif, and donating the usufruct. According to them, it means restricting the corpus such that ownership is transferred to God. The author then clarifies that waqf can be upon the rich without immediate charity, citing that ultimately a perpetual pious purpose is required. Al-Sarakhsi defines waqf as restricting owned property from others. The passage ends by stating the locus (محل) of waqf is valuable property.

Key Terms
الوقف (al-waqf): Restricting the corpus of property and donating its usufruct, with a specific legal definition differing between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
حبس العين (habs al-ayn): Restricting the corpus (the property itself) from being sold, gifted, or inherited.
التصدق بالمنفعة (al-tasadduq bi al-manfa'ah): Giving away the usufruct (benefits, income) as charity to the beneficiaries.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what happens to the ownership of the corpus (عين) in a waqf?
A) It is transferred to the beneficiaries.
B) It remains with the waqif.
C) It transfers to the state.
D) It is annulled.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two definitions of waqf, but the later authority (mufta bihi) is the Sahibayn's view that ownership passes to Allah.

Waqf — Endowment
intermediate
6 min
Conditions of the Waqif and Requirement of Immediacy
Lists conditions of waqif and prohibition of conditional waqf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions of the waqif and explain why waqf cannot be suspended on a future condition.

Core Idea
Waqf must be immediate and unconditional; suspension upon a future event invalidates it.

In this passage, we learn the essential conditions for the person making a waqf (endowment). The waqif must be legally capable of donating, and the endowment must be made immediately without any condition. If the waqf is made dependent on a future event, it is void. This lesson explains these rules and their basis in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the waqif's conditions
List the personal qualifications required: free, sane, adult. These ensure the waqif has full legal capacity to donate property irrevocably.
2
Determine the nature of waqf
Recognize that waqf is an immediate transfer of ownership to Allah. It cannot be made contingent on a future uncertain event.
3
Apply the rule to examples
Work through the example: 'If my son arrives, my house is waqf for the poor.' When the condition occurs, the waqf does not become valid because it was suspended.
4
Note the exception
Understand that suspension upon an existing fact (e.g., 'If this house is mine') is actually immediate (tunjiz) because the condition is already true.
This is not true suspension; it is a statement of current reality.
5
Compare with nathr (vows)
See why waqf differs from vows: vows can be suspended because one can swear an oath on them, but waqf cannot because it is not used in oaths.
The root cause is that waqf is a binding dedication, not a personal commitment like a vow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشرائطه أهلية الواقف للتبرع من كونه حراً عاقلاً بالغاً، وأن يكون منجزاً غير معلق فإنه مما لا يصلح تعليقه بالشرط، فلو قال إن قدم ولدي فداري صدقة موقوفة على المساكين فجاء ولده لا تصير وقفاً. وذكر في جامع الفصولين الوقف فيما لا يصح تعليقه بالشرط في رواية فأشار أن فيه روايتين وجزم بصحة إضافته . وفي البزازية وتعليق الوقف بالشرط باطل وفي الخانية : ولو قال إذا جاء غد فأرضي صدقة موقوفة أو قال إذا ملكت هذه الأرض فهي صدقة موقوفة لا تعليق والوقف لا يحتمل التعليق بالخطر لأنه لا يحلف به فلا تعليق الهبة بخلاف النذر لأنه يحلف به ويحتمل التعليق .اهـ. فإذا جاء غد تعليق ووقفته غداً إضافة وقد بينا الفرق بينهما في شرحنا على المنار وفي لب الأصول. ولو قال وقفته إن شئت ثم قال شئت كان باطلاً للتعليق، أما لو قال شئت وجعلتها صدقة هذا صح الكلام المتصل بخلاف ما لو قال إن كانت هذه الدار في ملكي فهي صدقة موقوفة فظهر أنها كانت في ملكه وقت التكلم فإنها تصير وقفاً لأنه تعليق على أمر كائن وهو تنجيز؛ كذا في فتح القدير، وسيأتي تعليقه بالموت الخامس من شرائطه الملك وقت الوقف
And its conditions are the eligibility of the waqif for donation: that he be free, sane, adult; and that it be immediate, not suspended, for it does not admit suspension upon a condition. If he says: 'When my son arrives, my house is a charity waqf for the poor' and his son arrives, it does not become waqf. It is mentioned in Jami' al-Fusulayn that waqf is among things that cannot be suspended upon a condition in one narration, so he indicated there are two narrations, and he decided it is valid to affiliate it. In al-Bazzaziyya: suspension of waqf upon a condition is invalid. In al-Khaniyya: if he says 'When tomorrow comes, my land is a charity waqf' or says 'When I own this land, it is a charity waqf' - this is suspension, and waqf does not admit suspension due to risk because one does not make an oath upon it, so there is no suspension of gift, unlike vows because one makes oath upon it and it admits suspension. End. So 'when tomorrow comes' is suspension, and 'I will waqf it tomorrow' is affiliation (idafa). We have explained the difference between them in our commentary on al-Manar and in Lub al-Usul. And if he says 'I have waqfed it if you wish' then says 'I wish', it is invalid due to suspension. But if he says 'I have waqfed it' and then 'I have made it charity', this is valid as continuous speech, unlike if he says 'If this house is in my ownership, it is a charity waqf' and it transpires it was in his ownership at the time of speaking - then it becomes waqf because it is suspension upon an existing matter which is immediate. This is from Fath al-Qadir. And its suspension upon death will come. The fifth of its conditions: ownership at the time of waqf.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage enumerates the conditions of the waqif (person making the endowment) and emphasizes that waqf must be immediate and not suspended on a future condition. The waqif must be free, sane, and adult. If the waqf is made conditional (e.g., 'when my son arrives'), it is invalid. There is a nuance: if the condition is an existing fact (e.g., 'if this house is mine' and it is indeed his), it is considered immediate (tunjiz) and valid. Also, saying 'I will waqf tomorrow' is not suspension but rather a promise to waqf in the future (idafa). The passage distinguishes between ta'liq (suspension, invalid) and idafa (affiliation to a future time, which may be valid). It also notes that unlike vows (nathr), waqf cannot be suspended because it is not used in oaths.

Key Terms
التعليق بالشرط (al-ta'liq bi al-shart): Making the waqf conditional upon a future uncertain event; this invalidates waqf.
الإضافة (al-idafa): Affiliating the waqf to a future time, like saying 'I will waqf tomorrow'; this is valid as a promise to waqf, not as an actual waqf until the time comes.
التنجيز (al-tunjiz): Immediate execution; the waqf must take effect at the moment of declaration without any condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if someone says 'I have waqfed this house if you wish' and then the addressee says 'I wish'?
A) The waqf becomes valid immediately.
B) The waqf is invalid due to suspension.
C) The waqf is valid only if the addressee is poor.
D) The waqf becomes valid upon the addressee's consent.

Key Takeaway
Waqf must be unconditional and immediate; any suspension upon a future event invalidates the waqf.

Distinguishing Suspension (Ta'liq) from Affiliation (Idafa) in Waqf
Distinguishes between invalid suspension (ta'liq) and valid affiliation (idafa), and notes validity of suspension upon existing fact.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ta'liq (suspension) and idafa (affiliation) in waqf, and apply the ruling that waqf is valid when suspended upon an existing fact.

Core Idea
Saying 'I will waqf tomorrow' is a valid promise (idafa), but 'when tomorrow comes, my land is waqf' is invalid suspension (ta'liq).

This lesson clarifies a subtle but crucial distinction in Hanafi waqf law: the difference between suspending a waqf upon a future event (ta'liq) and merely affiliating it to a future time (idafa). Additionally, if a waqf is made conditional upon an existing fact, it is considered immediate and valid. Understanding this distinction prevents common errors in drafting waqf documents.

Guided Path
1
Define ta'liq and idafa
Ta'liq makes the waqf depend on a future uncertain event. Idafa affiliates the waqf to a future time without making it conditional. The waqf takes effect when that time arrives, but it is not suspended; it is a promise.
Idafa is valid as a promise; the actual waqf occurs at the specified future time.
2
Apply to examples
'If tomorrow comes, my land is waqf' is ta'liq (invalid). 'I will waqf my land tomorrow' is idafa (valid as a promise). The difference is in wording: the first is conditional, the second is merely a future commitment.
3
Examine the 'existing fact' exception
If the condition is an existing fact (e.g., 'If this house is mine' and it is already his), it is not true suspension but immediate (tunjiz). The waqf is valid immediately because the condition is already true.
This is not suspension upon a risk (khatar) but rather a declaration of fact.
4
Compare with nathr
Vows (nathr) can be suspended because one can make an oath on them. Waqf cannot because it is a binding dedication that must be certain.
The root cause is that waqf is compared to freeing a slave, which cannot be conditional.
5
Note practical implications
When drafting a waqf, avoid any conditional language. If you wish to delay the effect, use idafa (e.g., 'I will waqf it next month') but ensure that at the appointed time, you actually execute the waqf.
Idafa is a promise, not a binding waqf until the time comes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Takeaway

Condition of Ownership at Time of Waqf and Related Cases
Ruling statements on ownership condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition of ownership at the time of waqf and apply it to various scenarios such as usurpation, unauthorized waqf, pre-emption, and others.

Core Idea
Ownership at the moment of waqf is essential; later acquisition does not cure it.

The validity of a waqf (endowment) in the Hanafi school depends on several conditions. One of the most critical is that the waqif must own the property at the time he makes the waqf. This lesson explores this condition in depth, examining a series of case studies from the classical texts that illustrate how this rule applies in various situations.

Guided Path
1
The Core Rule
Identify the fifth condition of waqf: ownership at the time of waqf. If the waqif does not own the property when he declares the waqf, the waqf is invalid, even if he later acquires ownership.
This is a fundamental principle; no waqf can be established on property not owned at the moment of declaration.
2
Usurpation Example
Consider a person who usurps land (ghasb) and then waqfs it. Even if he later buys it from the owner, the waqf remains invalid because he did not own it at the time of waqf.
This directly illustrates the rule: ownership must be present at the instant of waqf.
3
Unauthorized Waqf (Fudooli) Exception
If someone waqfs another's property without authorization (fudooli), the waqf can become valid if the owner subsequently ratifies it, but only with a judge's decree and delivery. This is an exception, not a violation of the ownership condition.
The ratification relates back to perfect the action, but it requires judicial involvement.
4
Pre-emption and Debt Cases
If the waqif is a buyer of land and a pre-emptor (shafi') comes after the waqf, the pre-emptor can annul the waqf. Similarly, if a sick person whose debts exceed his wealth makes a waqf, it will be sold to pay debts and the waqf is annulled.
These cases show that ownership is not absolute; existing rights can override the waqf.
5
Other Relevant Cases
Review the remaining scenarios: waqf of invalidly purchased goods after possession (valid), making it a mosque (valid but pre-emptor can annul), waqf before possession (valid only if price paid), waqf with defects or options, and waqf of iqta' lands (only if owned).
Each case confirms that the rule is strictly applied, with nuanced exceptions that depend on the nature of ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس من شرائطه الملك وقت الوقف حتى لو غصب أرضاً فوقفها ثم اشتراها من مالكها ودفع الثمن إليه أو صالح على مال دفعه إليه لا تكون وقفاً لأنه إنما ملكها بعد أن وقفها. هذا على أنه هو الواقف أما لو وقف ضيعة غيره على جهات فبلغ الغير فأجازه جاز بشرط الحكم والتسليم أو عدمه على الخلاف الذي سنذكره، وهذا هو المراد بجواز وقف الفضولي فلو استحق الوقف بطل، وكذا لو جاء شفيعها بعد وقف المشتري، وكذا لو وقف المريض المديون الذي أحاط الدين بماله فإنه يباع وينقض الوقف، ولو وقف المبيع فاسداً بعد القبض صح وعليه القيمة للبائع، وكذا لو اتخذها مسجداً، وكذا لو جعلها مسجداً وجاء شفيعها نقض المسجدية. ولو وقفها المشتري قبل القبض إن نقد الثمن جاز الوقف وإلا فهو موقوف ولو اشترى أرضاً فوقفها ثم جاء مستحق فاستحقها وأجاز البيع بطل الوقف في قول محمد، ولو ضمن المستحق البائع جاز الوقف في قول محمد ؛ الكل في الخانية. ولو وهبت له أرض هبة فاسدة فقبضها ثم وقفها صح وعليه قيمتها، ولو اشترى أرضاً فوقفها ثم اطلع على عيب رجع بالنقصان ولا يلزمه أن يشتري به بدلاً لعدم دخول نقصان العيب في الوقف؛ كذا في الإسعاف. وفي الذخيرة لو اشترى على أن البائع بالخيار فيها فوفقها ثم أجاز البائع البيع لم يجز الوقف اهـ. ويتفرع على اشتراط الملك أنه لا يجوز وقف الإقطاعات إلا إذا كان الأرض مواتاً فأقطعها الإمام رجلاً أو كانت ملكاً للإمام فأقطعها رجلاً وأنه لا يجوز وقف أرض
The fifth of its conditions: ownership at the time of waqf, so that if he usurped land and then waqfed it, then bought it from its owner and paid the price, or settled for payment to him, it does not become waqf because he only owned it after he waqfed it. This is if he is the waqif. But if he waqfed the estate of another for certain purposes, and the other learned of it and authorized it, it is valid subject to the condition of judicial decree and delivery or not according to the difference to be mentioned. This is what is meant by the validity of waqf by a fudooli (unauthorized person). If the waqf property is reclaimed, it is void. Likewise if its pre-emptor comes after the purchaser's waqf. Likewise if a sick person who is in debt exceeding his wealth waqfs, then it is sold and the waqf is annulled. If he waqfs an invalidly purchased item after possession, it is valid and he owes the seller its value. Likewise if he makes it a mosque. Likewise if he makes it a mosque and its pre-emptor comes, the mosqueness is annulled. If the purchaser waqfs before possession, if he paid the price, the waqf is permissible; otherwise it is suspended. If he bought land and waqfed it, then a claimant came and claimed it and authorized the sale, the waqf is void according to Muhammad. If the claimant guarantees the seller, the waqf is permissible according to Muhammad. All in al-Khaniyya. If land is given to him as a defective gift, he took possession and then waqfed it, it is valid and he owes its value. If he bought land and waqfed it, then discovers a defect, he can reclaim the reduction and is not required to buy a substitute with it because the reduction does not enter the waqf. This is in al-Is'af. In al-Dhakhira: if he bought with a condition that the seller has an option, then waqfed it, then the seller authorized the sale, the waqf is not permissible. End. It branches from the condition of ownership that it is not permissible to waqf grants (iqta'at) unless the land is dead and the imam granted it to a man, or it was owned by the imam and he granted it to a man, and that it is not permissible to waqf land...
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage covers the fifth condition for waqf: the waqif must own the property at the moment of making the waqf. If he waqfs property he does not own, the waqf is invalid even if he later acquires it. An exception is the waqf by a fudooli (unauthorized person) which can be validated by subsequent authorization of the owner, but it requires a judge's ruling or delivery. The passage then lists numerous case examples: usurped property, pre-emption, waqf by a person in debt exceeding his wealth, waqf of invalidly purchased goods, waqf by a purchaser before possession, waqf of defective goods, and waqf of granted lands (iqta'). Each case has specific rulings detailed in the authoritative Hanafi texts like al-Khaniyya and al-Dhakhira. The underlying principle is that ownership at the time of waqf is essential.

Key Terms
الفضولي (al-fudooli): A person who acts on behalf of another without authorization; here, waqfs someone else's property.
الإقطاع (al-iqta'): Land granted by the imam (ruler) to an individual; such land may or may not be owned by the grantee, affecting its eligibility for waqf.
الشفيع (al-shafi'): Pre-emptor; someone with a right to buy the property before the waqf, which they can exercise even after waqf.
الموات (al-mawat): Dead (unowned, virgin) land that can be granted by the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The waqf is invalid because the sale was invalid.
B) The waqf is valid but he must pay the seller the value.
C) The waqf is suspended until the sale is ratified.
D) The waqf is valid only if he makes it a mosque.

Key Takeaway
Ownership at the moment of waqf is a non-negotiable condition; later acquisition, ratification, or rights of others cannot validate a waqf made without ownership.

Waqf — Endowment

Conditional Waqf (Ta'liq) is Invalid: The Hanafi Position
Explains that waqf cannot be conditional; distinguishes suspension from addition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why conditional waqf is invalid in the Hanafi school and distinguish between ta'liq and idafa.

Core Idea
Waqf does not tolerate suspension — conditional language invalidates it because waqf requires immediacy.

Waqf is a perpetual charity that must take effect immediately. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses the ruling when someone attempts to suspend the waqf on a future condition. The author clarifies that ta'liq (suspension) is invalid, unlike idafa (addition to a future time), and explains the underlying reasoning by analogy to gift and vow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making a conditional declaration of waqf (e.g., 'if you come, then it is waqf'). The ruling is batil (invalid) because waqf requires immediate effect.
Conditional waqf is void from the outset, not merely suspended.
2
Distinguish ta'liq from idafa
Ta'liq ties the waqf to an uncertain future event (e.g., 'if you come'), while idafa adds a fixed future time (e.g., 'tomorrow'). Idafa is valid; ta'liq is not.
The key is the certainty of the time: fixed time = valid, uncertain condition = invalid.
3
Trace the analogy (qiyas)
The author compares waqf to gift (hiba) and vow (nadhr). Both hiba and waqf cannot be conditional because one does not swear by them. Nadhr can be conditional because one swears by it.
This is istihsan: departing from qiyas jali (analogy to nadhr) to qiyas khafi (analogy to hiba).
4
Identify the exception: existing condition
If the condition is already fulfilled at the time of speaking (e.g., he already owns the property), then it is tanziz (actualization), not true ta'liq, and the waqf is valid.
This is not a suspension; it is a confirmation of an existing reality.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a statement like 'When I own this house, it is waqf,' if he owns it at the moment of speech, it is valid; if he does not yet own it, the declaration is batil even if he later acquires it.
The validity depends on the state at the time of declaration, not future fulfillment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يصح يجوز لأنه تعليقه كما لا يصح فأرضي صدقة موقوفة أو قال إذا ملكت هذه الأرض فهي صدقة موقوفة لا تعليق والوقف لا يحتمل التعليق بالخطر لأنه لا يحلف به فلا تعليق الهبة بخلاف النذر لأنه يحلف به ويحتمل التعليق .اهـ. فإذا جاء غد تعليق ووقفته غداً إضافة وقد بينا الفرق بينهما في شرحنا على المنار وفي لب الأصول. ولو قال وقفته إن شئت ثم قال شئت كان باطلاً للتعليق، أما لو قال شئت وجعلتها صدقة هذا صح الكلام المتصل بخلاف ما لو قال إن كانت هذه الدار في ملكي فهي صدقة موقوفة فظهر أنها كانت في ملكه وقت التكلم فإنها تصير وقفاً لأنه تعليق على أمر كائن وهو تنجيز؛ كذا في فتح القدير، وسيأتي تعليقه بالموت
It is valid? It is permissible because its suspension, as it is not valid... So my land is a charity waqf, or he said: When I own this land, it is a charity waqf - there is no suspension. Waqf does not tolerate suspension by risk because one does not swear by it, so there is no suspension of gift unlike a vow because one swears by it and it tolerates suspension. End. So 'when tomorrow comes' is suspension and 'I will stop it tomorrow' is addition, and we have explained the difference between them in our commentary on al-Manar and in Lub al-Usul. And if he said: I have stopped it if you wish, then he said: I wish, it is invalid due to suspension. But if he said: I wish and I have made it charity - this correct speech is connected, unlike if he said: If this house is in my ownership, then it is a charity waqf, and it appears that it was in his ownership at the time of speaking, then it becomes a waqf because it is a suspension upon an existing matter, which is actualization; thus in Fath al-Qadir, and will come its suspension upon death.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the ruling of conditional waqf (ta'liq). The author states that waqf does not accept conditional language because it is a form of charity that requires immediate effect. The text distinguishes between ta'liq (suspension on a future uncertain event) and idafa (addition to a future time). The latter is valid if the time is fixed. The ruling is that if someone says 'When I own this land, it is waqf' and he owns it at that moment, it becomes waqf because the condition is already fulfilled (it is an existing matter). However, if he says 'I have stopped it if you wish,' it is invalid because it is a true suspension. The author also compares to vows (nadhr) which do tolerate suspension. The commentary cites sources like Fath al-Qadir and al-Manar.

Key Terms
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspension of a legal disposition on a future uncertain event (e.g., 'if you come, then it is waqf')
إضافة (idafa): Adding a future time to the effectiveness of a disposition (e.g., 'it is waqf tomorrow')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone says: 'When I own this land, it is a charity waqf,' and he already owns it at the time of speaking, what is the ruling?
A) The waqf is invalid because of suspension
B) The waqf is valid because the condition is already fulfilled
C) The waqf is valid only if he repeats the statement after ownership
D) The waqf is suspended until he actually owns it

Key Takeaway
Conditional waqf is invalid in Hanafi law because waqf must take immediate effect; only if the condition is already satisfied at the time of declaration (tanziz) is it valid.

The Fifth Condition of Waqf: Ownership at the Time of Declaration
States the condition of ownership at time of waqf with examples and intra-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fifth condition of waqf and apply it to scenarios where ownership is lacking.

Core Idea
Waqf requires ownership at the moment of declaration; later acquisition does not retroactively validate it.

The fifth condition of a valid waqf is that the person declaring the waqf must own the property at the exact moment of the declaration. This lesson examines that condition through multiple examples, including the case of a usurper who later buys the land, the waqf by an unauthorized person (fuduli), and the special situation of a person under interdiction (mahjoor 'alayh). Understanding this condition prevents common errors such as assuming later ownership can cure a defective waqf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Read the opening sentence: 'الخامس من شرائطه الملك وقت الوقف'. The condition is that the waqif must own the property at the time of the waqf declaration.
2
Analyze the usurpation example
The text gives the example of someone who usurps land and later buys it after declaring it waqf. The ruling is that the waqf is invalid because ownership was acquired after the declaration.
This demonstrates that later acquisition does not retroactively validate the waqf.
3
Distinguish from fuduli's waqf
Contrast with the case where a fuduli (unauthorized person) declares waqf of another's property, and the owner later ratifies. The text notes that this is valid subject to conditions because ratification relates back? Actually, the text says 'جاز بشرط الحكم والتسليم' – it requires a judge's ruling and handover. This is distinct from the usurper's case.
The key difference: the fuduli does not claim ownership, whereas the usurper acts as if he owns it.
4
Examine the mahjoor dispute
The passage presents an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Hanifa holds that the disposition of a mahjoor 'alayh (interdicted for folly) is not effective, so his waqf is invalid. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say his waqf is valid but the judgment of effectiveness is problematic. A composite solution allows a judge to rule it valid.
This shows the condition of ownership interacts with capacity to dispose.
5
Apply to other cases
The text provides additional scenarios: waqf of sold property before delivery, waqf by a sick debtor, waqf of land with a defect, and waqf of iqta' lands. For each, assess whether ownership was present at the moment of waqf.
Practice identifying the condition in varied contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس من شرائطه الملك وقت الوقف حتى لو غصب أرضاً فوقفها ثم اشتراها من مالكها ودفع الثمن إليه أو صالح على مال دفعه إليه لا تكون وقفاً لأنه إنما ملكها بعد أن وقفها. هذا على أنه هو الواقف أما لو وقف ضيعة غيره على جهات فبلغ الغير فأجازه جاز بشرط الحكم والتسليم أو عدمه على الخلاف الذي سنذكره، وهذا هو المراد بجواز وقف الفضولي فلو استحق الوقف بطل، وكذا لو جاء شفيعها بعد وقف المشتري، وكذا لو وقف المريض المديون الذي أحاط الدين بماله فإنه يباع وينقض الوقف، ولو وقف المبيع فاسداً بعد القبض صح وعليه القيمة للبائع، وكذا لو اتخذها مسجداً، وكذا لو جعلها مسجداً وجاء شفيعها نقض المسجدية. ولو وقفها المشتري قبل القبض إن نقد الثمن جاز الوقف وإلا فهو موقوف ولو اشترى أرضاً فوقفها ثم جاء مستحق فاستحقها وأجاز البيع بطل الوقف في قول محمد، ولو ضمن المستحق البائع جاز الوقف في قول محمد ؛ الكل في الخانية. ولو وهبت له أرض هبة فاسدة فقبضها ثم وقفها صح وعليه قيمتها، ولو اشترى أرضاً فوقفها ثم اطلع على عيب رجع بالنقصان ولا يلزمه أن يشتري به بدلاً لعدم دخول نقصان العيب في الوقف؛ كذا في الإسعاف. وفي الذخيرة لو اشترى على أن البائع بالخيار فيها فوفقها ثم أجاز البائع البيع لم يجز الوقف اهـ. ويتفرع على اشتراط الملك أنه لا يجوز وقف الإقطاعات إلا إذا كان الأرض مواتاً فأقطعها الإمام رجلاً أو كانت ملكاً للإمام فأقطعها رجلاً وأنه لا يجوز وقف أرض يصح وقفه، وقد تقرر عنده بل هو فتوى وهي لا ترفع الخلاف وعندهما تصرفه غير نافذ فلهذا لا ي. أن الوقف عنده لا يلزم وحينئذ فصحته بالحكم غير ظاهرة عند الكل فإن الوقف صحيح عند أبي يوسف والحكم بنفاذ تصرف المحجور غير صحيح، وعند أبي حنيفة بالعكس فيكون الحكم بصحة هذا الوقف مركباً من المذهبين. وقد استشكله الإمام الطرسوسي حين وقف على وقفية سطر فيها حكم بصحة الوقف المذكور ولو كان الواقف محجوراً عليه للسفه ثم قال : ولكن رأيت في المنية مثل هذه الواقعة المركبة من مذهبين حيث قال لو قضى القاضي بشهادة الفساق على غائب أو بشهادة الحوز للإمام لأنه ليس بمالك لها - زاد في التتارخانية - ولا لمالكها . قال : وتفسير أرض الحوز أرض عجز صاحبها عن زراعتها وأداء خراجها فدفعها إلى الإمام لتكون منافعها جبراً للخراج اهـ. وتمامه في الخصاف. وذكر أيضاً أن الموهوب له لا يصح وقفه قبل القبض ولو قبض بعده والموصى له كذلك قبل الموت
The fifth of its conditions: ownership at the time of waqf, even if he usurped land and stopped it, then bought it from its owner and paid the price, or settled for money paid, it is not waqf because he only owned it after stopping it. This is when he is the waqif. But if he stopped another's estate for causes, and the other learned and ratified it, it is valid subject to the condition of judgment and handover or not, according to the difference we will mention. This is what is meant by validity of waqf by a fuduli. If the waqf is challenged, it becomes void. Similarly if its shuf'ah claimant comes after the purchaser's waqf. Similarly if a sick debtor whose debt surrounds his property stops it, it is sold and the waqf is rescinded. If a valid sale is stopped after delivery, it is valid and he pays its value to the seller. Similarly if he makes it a mosque and its shuf'ah claimant comes, the mosque status is rescinded. If the purchaser stops it before delivery, if he paid the price, the waqf is valid, otherwise it is suspended. If he bought land and stopped it, then a claimant came and claimed it and ratified the sale, the waqf is void in Muhammad's view. If the claimant guarantees the seller, the waqf is valid in Muhammad's view; all in al-Khaniyyah. If land was given to him as a void gift and he took possession and then stopped it, it is valid and he owes its value. If he bought land and stopped it, then discovered a defect, he recovers the reduction and is not required to buy a substitute with it because the defect reduction does not enter the waqf; thus in al-Is'af. In al-Dhakhirah: if he bought on condition that the seller has an option, and he stopped it, then the seller ratified the sale, the waqf is not valid. End. Branched from the condition of ownership: that it is not permissible to stop iqta' lands unless the land is dead and the Imam grants it to a man, or it was the Imam's property and he grants it to a man. And that it is not permissible to stop land... its stop is valid, and it is established with him but it is a fatwa and does not remove the disagreement. With them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) his disposition is not effective, so for this... that waqf with him is not binding, and then its validity by judgment is not apparent to all. For waqf is valid according to Abu Yusuf, and the judgment of the effectiveness of a interdicted person's disposition is not valid. According to Abu Hanifa, the opposite. So the judgment of the validity of this waqf is composite from the two schools. Imam al-Tarsusi found this problematic when he saw a waqf document containing a judgment of validity of the mentioned waqf even if the waqif was interdicted for folly. Then he said: But I saw in al-Munya such a composite incident from two schools where he said: If a judge gives judgment based on the testimony of immoral persons against an absent person, or based on testimony of possession for the Imam because he is not its owner - added in al-Tatarkhaniyyah - nor its owner. He said: The explanation of land of possession: land whose owner is unable to cultivate it and pay its kharaj, so he hands it to the Imam so that its benefits compensate for the kharaj. End. Its completion is in al-Khassaf. He also mentioned that the donee's waqf is not valid before delivery, even if he takes delivery afterwards, and similarly for the legatee before death.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage details the fifth condition of waqf: ownership at the time of the waqf declaration. The author provides numerous examples showing that if one does not own the property at the moment of waqf, the waqf is invalid. For instance, usurping land and then later buying it does not validate the waqf because ownership was acquired after the declaration. There is a discussion of waqf by a fuduli (unauthorized person) which can be validated by ratification of the owner, subject to conditions. The text also addresses scenarios involving waqf by a debtor, waqf of sold property before delivery, and waqf of property with a defect. The passage includes intra-Hanafi differences, particularly between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding waqf by a mahjoor 'alayh (interdicted person). The author mentions a composite ruling from the two schools that may allow such waqf if a judge rules on it. The section on أرض الحوز (land held by the Imam due to owner's inability to cultivate) clarifies that such land cannot be validly stopped without ownership.

Key Terms
الفضولي (al-fuduli): An unauthorized person who makes a contract on behalf of another without permission.
أرض الحوز (ard al-hawz): Land that the Imam takes into possession because the owner is unable to cultivate and pay kharaj, so its benefits go to the treasury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone usurps land, declares it as waqf, then later buys it from the owner, what is the ruling?
A) The waqf becomes valid upon purchase
B) The waqf is invalid because he did not own it at the time of waqf
C) The waqf is valid if the owner ratifies
D) The waqf is valid only if the purchase is immediate

Key Takeaway
Ownership at the moment of waqf is an indispensable condition; without it, the waqf is invalid regardless of later acquisition.

Seventh Condition: No Interdiction on the Waqif
States the ruling on waqf by an interdicted person and the effect of a judge's ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on waqf by a person interdicted for folly and explain the proof based on the nature of waqf as a gratuitous disposition.

Core Idea
A waqf by an interdicted person is invalid because waqf is a gratuitous disposition requiring legal capacity.

We now examine the seventh condition for a valid waqf: the founder must not be under legal interdiction (hajr) for folly (safah). This condition ensures that only those with full legal capacity can dedicate property irrevocably. The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the ruling and highlights a nuance from Abu Yusuf regarding the effect of a judge's ruling, but ultimately affirms the invalidity of such a waqf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
State the seventh condition: the waqif must not be interdicted for folly. This is a condition for the validity of waqf.
Interdiction (hajr) is a legal restriction on disposing of property due to minority or folly.
2
State the ruling
The waqf of an interdicted person is invalid (batil) because waqf is a gratuitous disposition (tabarru'), and the interdicted person lacks the capacity for such dispositions.
This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
3
Examine the proof
The proof is a legal reasoning (talil): waqf is a tabarru', and the mahjoor is not qualified for tabarru'. This is analogous to other gratuitous transfers like gifts.
The text explicitly refutes a contrary view by stating 'waqf is a gratuitous disposition and he is not qualified for it'.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf held that if the waqf is made on oneself or for a non-religious cause, it terminates unless a judge rules on it. However, the preferred view is absolute invalidity.
The text says 'according to the view of Abu Yusuf which is correct with the investigators' but then refutes it.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, a judge's permission does not validate the waqf of an interdicted person according to the relied-upon position.
The condition remains that the waqif must be legally competent at the time of dedication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السابع عدم الحجر على الواقف لسفه أو فإذا هي وهو جميع الدار؛ كذا أطلقه الخصاف. وينبغي أنه إذا وقفها في الحجر للسفه على نفسه ثم لجهة لا دین : تنقطع أن على قول أبي يوسف وهو الصحيح عند المحققين، وعند الكل إذا حكم به يصح حاكم؛ كذا في فتح القدير وهو مدفوع بأن الوقف تبرع وهو ليس من أهله
The seventh: absence of interdiction on the waqif for folly or... so it is all of the house; thus al-Khassaf stated it absolutely. And it should be that if he stops it while under interdiction for folly on himself, then for a cause of no religion, it terminates. That is according to the view of Abu Yusuf which is correct with the investigators. And according to all, if a judge rules on it, it becomes valid; thus in Fath al-Qadir. But it is refuted that waqf is a gratuitous disposition and he is not qualified for it.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage discusses the seventh condition: the waqif must not be under legal interdiction (hajr) for folly (safah). The text mentions a view from Abu Yusuf that if a person under interdiction makes a waqf on himself (i.e., for his own benefit) or for a cause that is not religious, it terminates. However, if a judge issues a ruling on the waqf, it becomes valid according to all. This is then critiqued: waqf is a gratuitous disposition (tabarru'), and the interdicted person lacks the capacity for such dispositions. The source cited is Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
الحجر (al-hajr): Legal interdiction preventing a person from disposing of property due to folly or minority
السفه (al-safah): Folly or prodigality leading to interdiction
تبرع (tabarru'): Gratuitous disposition without compensation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is waqf by a person interdicted for folly invalid according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) Because the waqf is not witnessed
B) Because waqf is a gratuitous disposition and the interdicted person is not qualified for it
C) Because the waqf must be in writing
D) Because the waqif must be at least 18 years old

Key Takeaway
The absence of interdiction (hajr) is a condition for valid waqf; a waqf by an interdicted person is invalid because waqf is a gratuitous disposition.

Waqf with Option Condition: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Discusses validity of waqf with a condition of option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on waqf with khiyar al-shart and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
The validity of a waqf with an option condition varies: Muhammad invalidates, Abu Yusuf distinguishes known/unknown time, al-Samti validates and voids the condition.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq examines the ninth condition for waqf—that it must not be contingent on an option condition (khiyar al-shart). The Hanafi school does not have a single view; a three-way dispute is recorded between Imam Muhammad, Abu Yusuf, and al-Samti. Understanding these positions is crucial for determining the practical ruling in contemporary waqf cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling
Determine the exact legal issue: Is a waqf valid when the donor retains an option to revoke within a specified period?
This is the condition of khiyar al-shart.
2
State Imam Muhammad's position
Muhammad holds that such a waqf is invalid regardless of whether the option period is known or unknown. This is the strict view favored by Hilal.
Based on the binding nature of waqf.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf distinguishes: if the option time is known, both the waqf and the condition are valid by analogy to sale; if unknown, the waqf is void.
Qiyas jaliy to sale.
4
State al-Samti's position
Al-Samti validates the waqf absolutely and voids the condition only. This is supported by the text from al-Khaniyyah and later preferred.
Condition is treated like a void stipulation in a contract.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The preferred view for practice is al-Samti's: waqf valid, condition void. This is derived from al-Khaniyyah and al-Bahr al-Raiq.
Tarjih authority: later Hanafi masters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التاسع أن لا يلحق به خیار شرط فلو وقف على أنه بالخيار لم يصح عند محمد معلوماً كان الوقت أو مجهولاً، واختاره هلال. وقال أبو يوسف : إن كان الوقت معلوماً جاز الوقف والشرط كالبيع وإلا بطل الوقف، وصححه السمتي مطلقاً وأبطل الشرط. وظاهر ما في الخانية أنه لو جعل داره مسجداً على أنه بالخيار صح الوقف وبطل الشرط بلا خلاف. وقال الفقيه أبو جعفر : ينبغي على قول أبي يوسف فيما إذا كان الوقت مجهولاً أن الوقف ويبطل الشرط
The ninth: that he does not attach to it a condition of option. So if he stops on the condition that he has an option, it is not valid according to Muhammad, whether the time is known or unknown, and Hilal chose this. Abu Yusuf said: If the time is known, the waqf and the condition are valid like sale; otherwise the waqf is void. Al-Samti validated it absolutely and voided the condition. The apparent in al-Khaniyyah is that if he makes his house a mosque on the condition that he has an option, the waqf is valid and the condition is void without disagreement. Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far said: According to Abu Yusuf's view when the time is unknown, the waqf stands and the condition is void.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage discusses the ninth condition: the waqf must not have an option condition (khiyar al-shart). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Muhammad says such a waqf is invalid whether the option period is known or unknown. Hilal chose this. Abu Yusuf distinguishes: if the option period is known, both the waqf and the condition are valid by analogy to sale; if unknown, the waqf is void. Al-Samti validates the waqf absolutely and voids only the condition. The text from al-Khaniyyah indicates that if one makes his house a mosque with an option, the mosque waqf is valid and the condition is void by consensus. Abu Ja'far reconciles Abu Yusuf's position: when the time is unknown, the waqf is valid and the condition is void.

Key Terms
خيار شرط (khiyar al-shart): A condition in a contract allowing one party to rescind within a specified period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what is the ruling if someone makes a waqf with a condition that he has an option for one day?
A) The waqf is valid because the time is known
B) The waqf is invalid regardless of time
C) The waqf is valid and the condition is void
D) The waqf is suspended until the option expires

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has multiple views on waqf with option; the preferred position validates the waqf and voids the condition.

The Tenth Condition of Waqf: Perpetuity (Mu'abbad)
States the tenth condition: waqf must be perpetual.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on temporary waqf and explain why it is invalid.

Core Idea
A waqf is invalid if time-bound because waqf requires perpetuity.

Waqf is a perpetual charitable endowment. One of its essential conditions is that it must not be limited to a specific time. This short passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq establishes that any temporary waqf — whether for a day, a month, or a year — is legally void. Let's examine why.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is declaring a waqf with a time limit (e.g., 'for one year'). The Hanafi ruling is that such a waqf is invalid (batil).
The passage uses the term 'la yajuz' (not permissible) for a day or month, and 'bāṭil' (void) for a year.
2
Understand the condition of perpetuity
Waqf by definition is perpetual (mu'abbad). If the founder imposes a time limit, the endowment loses its essential character and becomes invalid.
Perpetuity is the tenth condition listed in the text.
3
Recognize the application to any time limit
The ruling applies to all fixed terms, whether short (day, month) or long (year). The duration does not matter; any temporal limitation invalidates the waqf.
Al-Khassaf's example covers both short and long periods.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi nuance
Hilal made a distinction (fasl) — possibly between waqf for an individual and waqf for a charitable purpose — but the text does not elaborate. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that all temporary waqf is invalid.
This distinction is not widely adopted; al-Khassaf's view is authoritative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العاشر أن لا يكون موقتاً قال الخصاف لو وقف داره يوماً أو شهراً لا يجوز لأنه لم يجعله مؤبداً، وكذا لو قال على فلان سنة كان باطلاً. وفصل هلال
The tenth: that it is not temporary. Al-Khassaf said: If he stops his house for a day or a month, it is not permissible because he did not make it perpetual. Similarly if he said 'for so-and-so for a year', it is void. And Hilal made a distinction.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This brief passage states the tenth condition: waqf must be perpetual (mu'abbad). If one limits the waqf to a specific period like a day, month, or year, it is invalid because the essence of waqf is perpetuity. The author references al-Khassaf and mentions that Hilal (a Hanafi scholar) made a distinction (perhaps between waqf for individuals and for a charitable purpose, but the text does not elaborate).

Key Terms
مؤبد (mu'abbad): Perpetual, without time limit
موقت (muwaqqat): Time-limited, temporary
باطل (bāṭil): Void, having no legal effect

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Khassaf, what is the ruling if a person says: 'I stop my house as waqf for a year'?
A) It is valid, because a year is a long enough period.
B) It is invalid, because waqf must be perpetual.
C) It is valid only if the house is used for a mosque.
D) It is invalid unless the beneficiary is a relative.

Key Takeaway
A waqf must be perpetual; any time limit makes it void.

Condition of Qurbah for a Dhimmi's Waqf
Notes that for a dhimmi, waqf must be a pious act

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that a dhimmi's waqf must be a pious act in his own religion and apply it to determine the validity of a dhimmi's endowment.

Core Idea
A dhimmi's waqf is only valid if its purpose is qurbah in his own faith.

This brief commentary note from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a critical refinement to the general rules of waqf. While a Muslim's waqf is always presumed to be a pious act (qurbah), a dhimmi (non-Muslim subject) must meet an additional condition: the waqf must be considered a pious act according to his own religion. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the Hanafi rulings on charitable endowments by non-Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the condition
Recognize that the passage addresses the validity of a dhimmi's waqf. The general ruling is that waqf is valid, but an extra condition (shart) is introduced: the purpose must be qurbah.
The phrase 'بشرط كونه قربة' indicates a condition.
2
Define 'qurbah' in this context
Understand that qurbah means a pious act that brings one closer to God. For a dhimmi, it must be qurbah according to his own religious beliefs, not necessarily Islamic standards.
The commentary says 'عندنا وعندهم'—according to us and according to them.
3
Apply the condition to a scenario
Given a specific dhimmi waqf, determine if the purpose is considered qurbah in that person's faith. If yes, the waqf is valid; if not, it is invalid.
This distinguishes dhimmi waqf from Muslim waqf, where the purpose is always assumed to be qurbah.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some scholars require the waqf to also be qurbah in Islam. The Hanafi position, as stated, only requires it to be qurbah in the dhimmi's own religion.
This is an ikhtilaf to be aware of.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (بشرط) كونه قربة عندنا وعندهم الظاهر أن هذا شرط في وقف الذمي
His saying: (by condition) it being a pious act according to us and according to them. The apparent is that this is a condition in the waqf of a dhimmi.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This brief note from the commentary (likely from al-Nahr or similar) addresses the condition that the waqf must be a pious act (qurbah). For a Muslim, all waqf is presumed pious. For a dhimmi (non-Muslim subject), the waqf must be a pious act according to his own religion for it to be valid. This is an additional condition specific to non-Muslims.

Key Terms
قربة (qurbah): An act that brings one closer to God; a pious or meritorious act.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under Muslim rule with a covenant of protection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What additional condition applies to the waqf of a dhimmi (non-Muslim subject)?
A) The waqf must be for a mosque
B) The waqf must be a pious act in his religion
C) The waqf must be for a family member
D) The waqf must be perpetual

Key Takeaway
A dhimmi's waqf is only valid if its purpose constitutes a pious act (qurbah) in his own religion.

Condition 6: Absence of Ignorance in Waqf Property
Explaining the sixth condition for valid waqf: specification must be clear

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of absence of ignorance in waqf and distinguish between invalidating ambiguity and permissible generality by istihsan.

Core Idea
A waqf must clearly specify the property; ambiguity invalidates it, except when waqfing an entire share by istihsan.

This lesson examines the sixth condition for a valid waqf: the property must be specified with certainty. The Hanafi school emphasizes that any ambiguity (jahalah) in describing the waqf property renders the waqf void. However, the school also applies istihsan to permit waqf of an entire undivided share without detailing fractional portions, because the intention is clear despite the lack of numerical specification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Determine that the condition is 'absence of ignorance' (عدمالجهالة) in specifying the waqf property. Ignorance here means uncertainty about what is being waqfed.
This is a shart (condition) for validity, not a rukn.
2
Apply the general rule to ambiguous cases
Understand that vague expressions like 'something from my land' or 'this land' without further identification cause invalidity because they fail to specify the subject matter clearly.
The text gives explicit examples of such invalid formulations.
3
Recognize the istihsan exception
Note that when a person waqfs 'all my share' of a specific property without stating the fractional portion, the waqf is valid by istihsan. This is because the share is known even if the fraction is not stated.
Istihsan overrides the general rule against ambiguity in this context.
4
Analyze the effect of specifying a fraction
If a person says 'I make my share a waqf, one third of the half,' the entire share becomes waqf, not just the fraction, because the mention of the fraction is ambiguous and the default is to treat it as the whole.
This ruling prevents uncertainty about the intended amount.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادس عدم الجهالة فلو وقف من أرضه شيئاً ولم يسمه كان باطلاً لأن الشيء يتناول القليل والكثير ولو بين بعد ذلك ربما يبين شيئاً قليلاً لا يوقف عادة، فلو وقف جميع حصته من هذه الدار والأرض ولم يسم السهام جاز استحساناً؛ كذا في الإسعاف ولو وقف هذه الأرض أو هذه الأرض وبين وجه الصرف كان باطلاً لمكان الجهالة. ولو قال جعلت نصيبي من هذه الدار وقفاً ثلث النصف كان الكل وقفاً وتمامه في الخانية
The sixth: absence of ignorance. If he waqfs something from his land without naming it, it is invalid because 'something' includes little and much, and if he specifies later, he might specify a little that is not usually waqfed. If he waqfs all his share from this house and land without specifying the portions, it is valid by istihsan; likewise in al-Is'af. If he waqfs 'this land' or 'this land' and specifies the direction of expenditure, it is invalid due to ignorance. If he says 'I have made my share of this house a waqf, one third of the half', the whole becomes waqf, and its completion is in al-Khaniyya.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage discusses the sixth condition for the validity of a waqf: the absence of ignorance (jahalah) in specifying the property. The author gives several examples demonstrating that ambiguity invalidates the waqf. If a person says 'I waqf something from my land' without naming it, the waqf is void because 'something' is vague and could be a negligible amount. However, if he waqfs his entire share from a specific house or land without stating the fractional share, it is valid by istihsan (juristic preference) because the intention is clear. The text also rules that specifying only the direction of expenditure (e.g., 'this land for such-and-such purpose') without identifying the land itself is invalid. Finally, if a person says 'my share of this house is a waqf, one third of the half', the entire share becomes waqf, not just the fraction; this is because the mention of the fraction is ambiguous and the default is to treat it as all.

Key Terms
الجهالة (al-jahalah): Ignorance or ambiguity in specifying the property or its details, which invalidates the waqf.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that allows waqf of an entire share without specifying portions, overriding the general rule against ambiguity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if someone says, 'I waqf something from my land' without naming it?
A) The waqf is valid because waqf is a virtuous act.
B) The waqf is invalid due to ignorance (jahalah).
C) The waqf is valid if he later specifies a reasonable amount.
D) The waqf is valid only if he intends the majority of the land.

Key Takeaway
A waqf must clearly identify the property; ambiguity invalidates, but waqf of an entire known share is valid by istihsan even without specifying the fraction.

Condition 8: No Condition of Selling the Waqf
Ruling that waqf with a condition allowing sale is invalid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a waqf with a condition of sale and distinguish it from a condition of substitution (istibdal).

Core Idea
A waqf with a condition of sale for personal benefit is invalid; a condition of substitution (istibdal) is valid.

This passage addresses a critical condition of waqf: the waqif must not stipulate the right to sell the waqf property for personal use. The Hanafi school, following Hilal and al-Khassaf, deems such a condition invalidating, while an early Hanafi jurist, Yusuf ibn Khalid al-Samti, allowed it by analogy to manumission. Understanding this distinction is key to ensuring the perpetuity of waqf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Identify the specific condition under scrutiny: stipulating the right to sell the waqf property and spend the proceeds for personal needs.
2
State the Hanafi majority position
According to Hilal and al-Khassaf (the chosen/mukhtar view), such a waqf is invalid (batil).
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi counter-view
Yusuf ibn Khalid al-Samti permits the condition by analogy (qiyas) to manumission ('itq), where a condition of sale is allowed.
This view is not relied upon.
4
Explain the distinction with istibdal
A condition of substitution (istibdal)—exchanging waqf property for another—does not invalidate the waqf, as it maintains the perpetual nature of the endowment.
This distinction is crucial for practice.
5
Apply the ruling
Given a waqf scenario, determine whether the condition is a sale for personal benefit (invalid) or a substitution for the waqf's benefit (valid).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثامن أن لا يذكر مع الوقف اشتراط بيعه فلو وقف بشرط أن يبيعها ويصرف ثمنها إلى حاجته لا يصح الوقف في المختار ؛ كذا في البزازية وهو قول هلال والخصاف. وجوزه يوسف بن خالد السمتي إلحاقاً للوقف بالعتق، وأما اشتراط الاستبدال فلا يبطله كما سيأتي في محله.
The eighth: that he does not mention with the waqf a stipulation of selling it. For if he makes a waqf with a condition that he sells it and spends its price for his need, the waqf is invalid in the chosen view; so in al-Bazzaziyya, and it is the saying of Hilal and al-Khassaf. Yusuf ibn Khalid al-Samti allowed it, analogizing waqf to manumission. As for stipulating substitution (istibdal), it does not invalidate the waqf, as will come in its place.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage covers the eighth condition: no condition of selling the waqf property. If a person makes a waqf but stipulates that he can sell it and use the proceeds for himself, the waqf is invalid according to the chosen (mukhtar) position. This is the view of Hilal and al-Khassaf. However, Yusuf ibn Khalid al-Samti permitted such a condition, drawing an analogy to manumission where a condition of sale is allowed? The text then clarifies that stipulating substitution (istibdal) i.e., exchanging the waqf property for another, does not invalidate the waqf. This distinction is important: a condition of sale for personal benefit invalidates, but a condition of substitution for the benefit of the waqf is permissible.

Key Terms
اشتراط بيعه (ishtirat bay'ihi): Stipulating the right to sell the waqf property, which invalidates the waqf.
الاستبدال (al-istibdal): Substitution of waqf property with another; permissible without invalidating the waqf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person makes a waqf with a condition that he can sell the property and spend the price for his own needs?
A) The waqf is valid and the condition is void.
B) The waqf is invalid according to the chosen view.
C) The waqf is valid according to all scholars.
D) The waqf is valid if the condition is for a charitable purpose.

Key Takeaway
A waqf with a condition that the waqif can sell the property for personal benefit is invalid in the Hanafi school, but a condition of substitution (istibdal) is permissible.
